Man, the sheer amount of wasted potential the Star Wars series has is just depressing. Beyond the original trilogy, IMHO only the video games and the novels - well, some of them xD - really make imaginative and inspired use of the setting and lore; the "reference" books are also brilliant worldbuilding, in fact some of the best worldbuilding ever (as a kid I used to love poring over those incredibly detailed "exploded" diagrams of ships and their interiors, engines, power sources etc.). It's nominally satisfying to see Star Wars back on the screen in a significant way, but apart from that the Disney acquisition has been a constant downward spiral of disappointment with only a few glimmers of originality and intrigue, largely a consequence of an unfocused and floundering creative vision that all too often succumbs to emotionally hollow nostalgia.   A demonstrative example of this creatively bankrupt obsession with the past is the fact that Tatooine the predominant setting for FOUR of the Disney+ series, despite already being a highly important location in "A New Hope", "Return of the Jedi" and "The Phantom Menace".  The Star Wars galaxy is supposedly massive, and yet we're constantly constrained to a single aesthetically nondescript desert location that could easily be any desert on Earth; there's very little that's alien, otherworldly or awe-inspiring about it, unlike say the planet-encompassing city of Coruscant, or the incredible verdant vistas of Naboo and its distinctive dome-riddled architectural style.  Show us something new! Show us the homeworld of one of the many recurring alien species, like the Twilek, the Cereans, the Vurk, the Quermian, the Togruta or the Zabrak (hell, just SHOW us more aliens in general, and make them main characters ffs)! It's genuinely insane that they have such an expansive setting yet they squander it with this constant recycling of characters and places and plots and themes and even twists. It's almost like they're intentionally trying to make it as uninteresting as they possibly can, it's just so bizarre.   Such a waste of an immersive fictional universe! Remember this guy? Remember this guy? Remember this not-so-secret map that gives you the exact coordinates of the villain's main base for some weird reason (who is actually making these maps in the first place?!), it's not like we've ever used this plot device before?  The series has lost its most vital ingredient - a sense of wonder. And I don't think it's ever gonna get it back, not unless there's a radical overhaul of Disney's creative team, because whoever they've got on that team right now probably doesn't even have the word "creative" in their vocabulary. Lifeless corporate stooges will write lifeless corporate stories. Such a shame.

I'm alright with what Sabine did in this season. It's her Jedi lineage's way. From dooku to qui gon to obi wan to Anakin to ahsoka to Sabine, they were always more emotional and unorthodoxed in their ways and the way they approached a plan of action.
The ahsoka show was all about the Yoda, dooku, qui gon, obi wan, Anakin, ahsoka, Sabine Jedi lineage and legacy. It was meant to demonstrate that this Jedi training and strategies were far from the norm and meant to let the fans know, that these Jedis valued different things, like friendship and were more emotionally concerned and risked their lives in unorthodoxed ways than the typical Jedi would approach a given situation. Sabine risking everything to find Ezra, is in keeping with what this jedi's lineage of Jedi masters gambits.
